## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate-law ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of concentration A, so the task is to infer a kinetic rate law of the form dA_dt = f(A, t). With only t and A available, common candidates are empirical/elementary-order decay laws, equilibrium-relaxation forms, and time-varying (e.g., catalysis/temperature-programmed) effective rate constants k(t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when reactant is in excess or surface-limited)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular 2A -> products or pseudo-second-order)
- General power-law (nth-order): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Equilibrium relaxation (linear driving force): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (first-order approach to steady-state/equilibrium A=c1)
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating with depletion: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (sigmoidal time-course from autocatalysis or limited capacity)
- Cubic inhibition/auto-inhibition: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (A - c1) * (A - c2) (multiple steady states, bistability-like kinetics)
- Time-programmed first-order (linear k(t)): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant drifting with time, e.g., catalyst activation/deactivation)
- Time-programmed first-order (exponential k(t)): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (accelerating/decaying effective rate constant over time)
- Reciprocal-time effective rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (t + c1) (aging/relaxation processes where apparent rate slows as 1/(t+offset))
- Periodic modulation of rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (externally driven/oscillatory environment affecting kinetics)
- Source/sink with baseline production: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant input with first-order removal; reaches steady state A=c0/c1 structurally)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Monotone decay of A with no steady state above zero often maps to dA_dt being strictly negative for A>0 (e.g., -c0*A, -c0*A**n).
- If the half-life is approximately constant across A, the structure dA_dt ∝ -A (first-order) is favored; if half-life shortens at high A, dA_dt ∝ -A**n with n>1 is favored.
- Observed approach of A(t) to a nonzero plateau suggests a driving-force form dA_dt = -c0*(A - c1) or addition of a source term c0 - c1*A.
- Sigmoidal A(t) (slow-fast-slow) can arise from autocatalytic terms like c0*A*(c1-A) that change sign or peak at intermediate A.
- A strong early-time transient that cannot be explained by A-dependence alone suggests k(t) modulation, e.g., (c0+c1*t) or exp(c1*t) multiplying A.
- Apparent rate slowing over time at similar A levels suggests k(t) decreasing with t (e.g., proportional to 1/(t+c1) or exp(-c*t) variants).
- If dA_dt periodically changes magnitude at fixed A, include sinusoidal modulation in k(t): A * (1 + c*sin(c*t)).
- Multiple observed stable levels (or switching behavior) in A can be modeled by polynomial factors in A creating multiple fixed points, e.g., -A*(A-c1)*(A-c2).

1. `sqrt(A)` — a square root term

- `sqrt(A)` is a specific basis function that cannot be replicated by polynomials, rationals, exponentials, or logarithms.
- `sin(c*A)` is a specific basis function that cannot be replicated by polynomials, rationals, or exponentials.

Let me check which candidates have both `sin` and `sqrt` (or equivalent) terms:
